logFuncName, absAddr)\n336: \t\treturn nil\n337: \t}\n338: \n339: \tif obj != nil {\n340: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] %s: writing state object for %s\", logFuncName, absAddr)\n341: \t} else {\n342: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] %s: removing state object for %s\", logFuncName, absAddr)\n343: \t}\n344: \n345: \tschema, currentVersion := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(absAddr.ContainingResource().Resource)\n346: \tif schema == nil {\n347: \t\t// It shouldn't be possible to get this far in any real scenario\n348: \t\t// without a schema, but we might end up here in contrived tests that\n349: \t\t// fail to set up their world properly.\n350: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to encode %s in state: no resource type schema available\", absAddr)\n351: \t}\n352: \n353: \tsrc, err := obj.Encode(schema.ImpliedType(), currentVersion)\n354: \tif err != nil {\n355: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to encode %s in state: %s\", absAddr, err)\n356: \t}\n357: \n358: \twrite(src)\n359: \treturn nil\n360: }\n361: \n362: // planDestroy returns a plain destroy diff.\n363: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) planDestroy(ctx EvalContext, currentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject, deposedKey states.DeposedKey) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n364: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n365: \tvar plan *plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n366: \n367: \tabsAddr := n.Addr\n368: \n369: \tif n.ResolvedProvider.Provider.Type == \"\" {\n370: \t\tif deposedKey == \"\" {\n371: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"planDestroy for %s does not have ProviderAddr set\", absAddr))\n372: \t\t} else {\n373: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"planDestroy for %s (deposed %s) does not have ProviderAddr set\", absAddr, deposedKey))\n374: \t\t}\n375: \t}\n376: \n377: \t// If there is no state or our attributes object is null then we're already\n378: \t// destroyed.\n379: \tif currentState == nil || currentState.Value.IsNull() {\n380: \t\t// We still need to generate a NoOp change, because that allows\n381: \t\t// outside consumers of the plan to distinguish between us affirming\n382: \t\t// that we checked something and concluded no changes were needed\n383: \t\t// vs. that something being entirely excluded e.g. due to -target.\n384: \t\tnoop := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n385: \t\t\tAddr:        absAddr,\n386: \t\t\tPrevRunAddr: n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n387: \t\t\tDeposedKey:  deposedKey,\n388: \t\t\tChange: plans.Change{\n389: \t\t\t\tAction: plans.NoOp,\n390: \t\t\t\tBefore: \t\t\tPlannedState: nullVal,\n423: \t\t}\n424: \t} else {\n425: \t\t// Allow the provider to check the destroy plan, and insert any\n426: \t\t// necessary private data.\n427: \t\tresp = have a config for all destroys, but we want to reference\n437: \t\t// it in the diagnostics if we do.\n438: \t\tif n.Config != nil {\n439: \t\t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(n.Config.Config, n.Addr.String())\n440: \t\t}\n441: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(resp.Diagnostics)\n442: \t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n443: \t\t\treturn plan, diags\n444: \t\t}\n445: \n446: \t\t// Check that the provider returned a null value here, since that is the\n447: \t\t// only valid value for a destroy plan.\n448: \t\tif !resp.PlannedState.IsNull() {\n449: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n450: \t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n451: \t\t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid plan\",\n452: \t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n453: \t\t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned a non-null destroy value for %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n454: \t\t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr),\n455: \t\t\t),\n456: \t\t\t)\n457: \t\t\treturn plan, diags\n458: \t\t}\n459: \t}\n460: \n461: \t// Plan is always the same for a destroy.\n462: \tplan = &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n463: \t\tAddr:        absAddr,\n464: \t\tPrevRunAddr: n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n465: \t\tDeposedKey:  deposedKey,\n466: \t\tChange: plans.Change{\n467: \t\t\tAction: plans.Delete,\n468: \t\t\tBefore: currentState.Value,\n469: \t\t\tAfter:  nullVal,\n470: \t\t},\n471: \t\tPrivate:      resp.PlannedPrivate,\n472: \t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n473: \t}\n474: \n475: \treturn plan, diags\n476: }\n477: \n478: // planForget returns a Forget change.\n479: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) planForget(ctx EvalContext, currentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject, deposedKey states.DeposedKey) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n480: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n481: \tvar plan *plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n482: \n483: \tabsAddr := n.Addr\n484: \n485: \t// If there planned change for an instance object into the set of\n526: // global planned changes.\n527: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) writeChange(ctx EvalContext, change *plans.ResourceInstanceChange, deposedKey states.DeposedKey) error {\n528: \tchanges := ctx.Changes()\n529: \n530: \tif change == nil {\n531: \t\t// Caller sets nil to indicate that we need to remove a change from\n532: \t\t// the set of changes.\n533: \t\tchanges.RemoveResourceInstanceChange(n.Addr, deposedKey)\n534: \t\treturn nil\n535: \t}\n536: \n537: \t_, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n538: \tif err != nil {\n539: \t\treturn err\n540: \t}\n541: \n542: \tif change.Addr.String() != n.Addr.String() || change.DeposedKey != deposedKey {\n543: \t\t// Should never happen, and indicates a bug in the caller.\n544: \t\tpanic(\"inconsistent address and/or deposed key in writeChange\")\n545: \t}\n546: \tif change.PrevRunAddr.Resource.Resource.Type == \"\" {\n547: \t\t// Should never happen, and indicates a bug in the caller.\n548: \t\t// (The change.Encode function actually has its own fixup to just\n549: \t\t// quietly make this match change.Addr in the incorrect case, but we\n550: \t\t// intentionally panic here in order to catch incorrect callers where\n551: \t\t// the stack trace will hopefully be actually useful. The tolerance\n552: \t\t// at the next layer down is mainly to accommodate sloppy input in\n553: \t\t// older tests.)\n554: \t\tpanic(\"unpopulated ResourceInstanceChange.PrevRunAddr in writeChange\")\n555: \t}\n556: \n557: \tri := n.Addr.Resource\n558: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(ri.Resource)\n559: \tif schema == nil {\n560: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n561: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"provider does not support resource type %q\", ri.Resource.Type)\n562: \t}\n563: \n564: \tcsrc, err := change.Encode(schema.ImpliedType())\n565: \tif err != nil {\n566: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to encode planned changes for %s: %s\", n.Addr, err)\n567: \t}\n568: \n569: \tchanges.AppendResourceInstanceChange(csrc)\n570: \tif deposedKey == states.NotDeposed {\n571: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] writeChange: recorded %s change for %s\", change.Action, n.Addr)\n572: \t} else {\n573: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] writeChange: recorded %s change for %s deposed object %s\", change.Action, n.Addr, deposedKey)\n574: \t}\n575: \n576: \treturn nil\n577: }\n578: \n579: // refresh does a refresh for a resource\n580: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) refresh(ctx EvalContext, deposedKey states.DeposedKey, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject) (*states.ResourceInstanceObject, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n581: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n582: \tabsAddr := n.Addr\n583: \tif deposedKey == states.NotDeposed {\n584: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] NodeAbstractResourceInstance.refresh for %s\", absAddr)\n585: \t} else {\n586: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] NodeAbstractResourceInstance.refresh for %s (deposed object %s)\", absAddr, deposedKey)\n587: \t}\n588: \tprovider, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n589: \tif err != nil {\n590: \t\treturn state, diags.Append(err)\n591: \t}\n592: \t// If we have no state, we don't do any refreshing\n593: \tif state == nil {\n594: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] refresh: %s: no state, so not refreshing\", absAddr)\n595: \t\treturn state, diags\n596: \t}\n597: \n598: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(n.Addr.Resource.ContainingResource())\n599: \tif schema == nil {\n600: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n601: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"provider does not support resource type %q\", n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type))\n602: \t\treturn state, diags\n603: \t}\n604: \n605: \tmetaConfigVal, metaDiags := n.providerMetas(ctx)\n606: \tdiags = diags.Append(metaDiags)\n607: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n608: \t\treturn state, diags\n609: \t}\n610: \n611: \t// Call pre-refresh hook\n612: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n613: \t\treturn h.PreRefresh(absAddr, deposedKey, state.Value)\n614: \t}))\n615: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n616: \t\treturn state, diags\n617: \t}\n618: \n619: \t// Refresh!\n620: \tpriorVal := state.Value\n621: \n622: \t// Unmarked before sending to provider\n623: \tvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\n624: \tif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n625: \t\tpriorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n626: \t}\n627: \n628: \tvar resp providers.ReadResourceResponse\n629: \tif n.override != nil {\n630: \t\t// If we have an override set for this resource, we don't want to talk\n631: \t\t// to the provider so we'll just return whatever was in state.\n632: \t\tresp = providers.ReadResourceResponse{\n633: \t\t\tNewState: priorVal,\n634: \t\t}\n635: \t} else {\n636: \t\tresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n637: \t\t\tTypeName:     n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n638: \t\t\tPriorState:   priorVal,\n639: \t\t\tPrivate:      state.Private,\n640: \t\t\tProviderMeta: metaConfigVal,\n641: \t\t})\n642: \t}\n643: \tif n.Config != nil {\n644: \t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(n.Config.Config, n.Addr.String())\n645: \t}\n646: \n647: \tdiags = diags.Append(resp.Diagnostics)\n648: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n649: \t\treturn state, diags\n650: \t}\n651: \n652: \tif resp.NewState == cty.NilVal {\n653: \t\t// This ought not to happen in real cases since it's not possible to\n654: \t\t// send NilVal over the plugin RPC channel, but it can come up in\n655: \t\t// tests due to sloppy mocking.\n656: \t\tpanic(\"new state is cty.NilVal\")\n657: \t}\n658: \n659: \tif !resp.NewState.IsWhollyKnown() {\n660: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n661: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n662: \t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid object\",\n663: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n664: \t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s during refresh: %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n665: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, absAddr, \"The returned state contains unknown values\",\n666: \t\t\t),\n667: \t\t))\n668: \t}\n669: \n670: \tfor _, err := range resp.NewState.Type().TestConformance(schema.ImpliedType()) {\n671: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n672: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n673: \t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid object\",\n674: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n675: \t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s during refresh: %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n676: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, absAddr, tfdiags.FormatError(err),\n677: \t\t\t),\n678: \t\t))\n679: \t}\n680: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n681: \t\treturn state, diags\n682: \t}\n683: \n684: \tnewState := objchange.NormalizeObjectFromLegacySDK(resp.NewState, schema)\n685: \tif !newState.RawEquals(resp.NewState) {\n686: \t\t// We had to fix up this object in some way, and we still need to\n687: \t\t// accept any changes for compatibility, so all we can do is log a\n688: \t\t// warning about the change.\n689: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[WARN] Provider %q produced an invalid new value containing null blocks for %q during refresh\\n\", n.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr)\n690: \t}\n691: \n692: \tret := state.DeepCopy()\n693: \tret.Value = newState\n694: \tret.Private = resp.Private\n695: \n696: \t// We have no way to exempt provider using the legacy SDK from this check,\n697: \t// so we can only log inconsistencies with the updated state values.\n698: \t// In most cases these are not errors anyway, and represent \"drift\" from\n699: \t// external changes which will be handled by the subsequent plan.\n700: \tif errs := objchange.AssertObjectCompatible(schema, priorVal, ret.Value); len(errs) > 0 {\n701: \t\tvar buf strings.Builder\n702: \t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"[WARN] Provider %q produced an unexpected new value for %s during refresh.\", n.ResolvedProvider.Provider.String(), absAddr)\n703: \t\tfor _, err := range errs {\n704: \t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"\\n      - %s\", tfdiags.FormatError(err))\n705: \t\t}\n706: \t\tlog.Print(buf.String())\n707: \t}\n708: \n709: \t// Call post-refresh hook\n710: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n711: \t\treturn h.PostRefresh(absAddr, deposedKey, priorVal, ret.Value)\n712: \t}))\n713: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n714: \t\treturn ret, diags\n715: \t}\n716: \n717: \t// Mark the value if necessary\n718: \tif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n719: \t\tret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n720: \t}\n721: \n722: \treturn ret, diags\n723: }\n724: \n725: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) plan(\n726: \tctx EvalContext,\n727: \tplannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange,\n728: \tcurrentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n729: \tcreateBeforeDestroy bool,\n730: \tforceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n731: ) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n732: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n733: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n734: \n735: \tresource := n.Addr.Resource.Resource\n736: \tprovider, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n737: \tif err != nil {\n738: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags.Append(err)\n739: \t}\n740: \n741: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(resource)\n742: \tif schema == nil {\n743: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n744: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"provider does not support resource type %q\", resource.Type))\n745: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n746: \t}\n747: \n748: \t// If we're importing and generating config, generate it now.\n749: \tif n.Config == nil {\n750: \t\t// This shouldn't happen. A node that isn't generating config should\n751: \t\t// have embedded config, and the rest of Terraform should enforce this.\n752: \t\t// If, however, we didn't do things correctly the next line will panic,\n753: \t\t// so let's not do that and return an error message with more context.\n754: \n755: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n756: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n757: \t\t\t\"Resource has no configuration\",\n758: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Terraform attempted to process a resource at %s that has no configuration. This is a bug in Terraform; please report it!\", n.Addr.String())))\n759: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n760: \t}\n761: \n762: \tconfig := *n.Config\n763: \n764: \tcheckRuleSeverity := tfdiags.Error\n765: \tif n.preDestroyRefresh {\n766: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity = tfdiags.Warning\n767: \t}\n768: \n769: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n770: \t\t// If we already planned the action, we stick to that plan\n771: \t\tcreateBeforeDestroy = plannedChange.Action == plans.CreateThenDelete\n772: \t}\n773: \n774: \t// Evaluate the configuration\n775: \tforEach, _ := evaluateForEachExpression(n.Config.ForEach, ctx)\n776: \n777: \tkeyData = EvalDataForInstanceKey(n.ResourceInstanceAddr().Resource.Key, forEach)\n778: \n779: \tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n780: \t\taddrs.ResourcePrecondition,\n781: \t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n782: \t\tctx, n.Addr, keyData,\n783: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n784: \t)\n785: \tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n786: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n787: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags // failed preconditions prevent further evaluation\n788: \t}\n789: \n790: \t// If we have a previous plan and the action was a noop, then the only\n791: \t// reason we're in this method was to evaluate the preconditions. would've ended up with a _create_ action this time,\n1216: \t// which we now need to paper over to get a result consistent with what\n1217: \t// we originally intended.\n1218: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n1219: \t\tprevChange := *plannedChange\n1220: \t\tif prevChange.Action.IsReplace() && action == plans.Create {\n1221: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] plan: %s treating Create change as %s change to match with earlier plan\", n.Addr, prevChange.Action)\n1222: \t\t\taction = prevChange.Action\n1223: \t\t\tpriorVal = prevChange.Before\n1224: \t\t}\n1225: \t}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Call post-refresh hook\n1228: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n1229: \t\treturn h.PostDiff(n.Addr, addrs.NotDeposed, action, priorVal, plannedNewVal)\n1230: \t}))\n1231: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1232: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1233: \t}\n1234: \n1235: \t// Update our return plan\n1236: \tplan := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1237: \t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n1238: \t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n1239: \t\tPrivate:      plannedPrivate,\n1240: \t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n1241: \t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1242: \t\t\tAction: reqRep,\n1252: \t}\n1253: \n1254: \t// Update our return state\n1255: \tstate := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1256: \t\t// We use the special \"planned\" status here to note that this\n1257: \t\t// object's value is not yet complete. In that case we just don't supply a\n1288: \t\t// schema and return the prior val directly.\n1289: \t\tif schema == nil {\n1290: \t\t\treturn prior, nil\n1291: \t\t}\n1292: \n1293: \t\t// If we are trying to ignore all attribute changes, we must filter\n1294: \t\t// computed attributes out from the prior state to avoid sending them\n1295: \t\t// to the provider as if they were included in the configuration.\n1296: \t\tret, _ := cty.Transform(prior, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1297: \t\t\tattr := schema.AttributeByPath(path)\n1298: \t\t\tif attr != nil && attr.Computed && !attr.Optional {\n1299: \t\t\t\treturn cty.NullVal(v.Type()), nil\n1300: \t\t\t}\n1301: \n1302: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1303: \t\t})\n1304: \n1305: \t\treturn ret, nil\n1306: \t}\n1307: \n1308: \tif prior.IsNull() || config.IsNull() {\n1309: \t\t// Ignore changes doesn't apply when we're creating for the first time.\n1310: \t\t// Proposed should never be null here, but if it is then we'll just let it be.\n1311: \t\treturn config, nil\n1312: \t}\n1313: \n1314: \tret, diags := processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config, ignoreChanges)\n1315: \n1316: \treturn ret, diags\n1317: }\n1318: \n1319: // Convert the hcl.Traversal values we get form the configuration to the\n1320: // cty.Path values we need to operate on the cty.Values\n1321: func traversalsToPaths(traversals []hcl.Traversal) []cty.Path {\n1322: \tpaths := make([]cty.Path, len(traversals))\n1323: \tfor i, traversal := range traversals {\n1324: \t\tpath := traversalToPath(traversal)\n1325: \t\tpaths[i] = path\n1326: \t}\n1327: \treturn paths\n1328: }\n1329: \n1330: func traversalToPath(traversal hcl.Traversal) cty.Path {\n1331: \tpath := make(cty.Path, len(traversal))\n1332: \tfor si, step := range traversal {\n1333: \t\tswitch ts := step.(type) {\n1334: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseRoot:\n1335: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1336: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1337: \t\t\t}\n1338: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseAttr:\n1339: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1340: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1341: \t\t\t}\n1342: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseIndex:\n1343: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.IndexStep{\n1344: \t\t\t\tKey: ts.Key,\n1345: \t\t\t}\n1346: \t\tdefault:\n1347: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unsupported traversal step %#v\", step))\n1348: \t\t}\n1349: \t}\n1350: \treturn path\n1351: }\n1352: \n1353: func processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config cty.Value, ignoreChangesPath []cty.Path) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1354: \ttype ignoreChange struct {\n1355: \t\t// Path is the full path, minus any trailing map index\n1356: \t\tpath cty.Path\n1357: \t\t// Value is the value we are to retain at the above path. If there is a\n1358: \t\t// key value, this must be a map and the desired value will be at the\n1359: \t\t// key index.\n1360: \t\tvalue cty.Value\n1361: \t\t// Key is the index key if the ignored path ends in a map index.\n1362: \t\tkey cty.Value\n1363: \t}\n1364: \tvar ignoredValues []ignoreChange\n1365: \n1366: \t// Find the actual changes first and store them in the ignoreChange struct.\n1367: \t// If the change was to a map value, and the key doesn't exist in the\n1368: \t// config, it would never be visited in the transform walk.\n1369: \tfor _, icPath := range ignoreChangesPath {\n1370: \t\tkey := cty.NullVal(cty.String)\n1371: \t\t// check for a map index, since maps are the only structure where we\n1372: \t\t// could have invalid path steps.\n1373: \t\tlast, ok := icPath[len(icPath)-1].(cty.IndexStep)\n1374: \t\tif ok {\n1375: \t\t\tif last.Key.Type() == cty.String {\n1376: \t\t\t\ticPath = icPath[:len(icPath)-1]\n1377: \t\t\t\tkey = last.Key\n1378: \t\t\t}\n1379: \t\t}\n1380: \n1381: \t\t// The structure should have been validated already, and we already\n1382: \t\t// trimmed the trailing map index. Any other intermediate index error\n1383: \t\t// means we wouldn't be able to apply the value below, so no need to\n1384: \t\t// record this.\n1385: \t\tp, err := icPath.Apply(prior)\n1386: \t\tif err != nil {\n1387: \t\t\tcontinue\n1388: \t\t}\n1389: \t\tc, err := icPath.Apply(config)\n1390: \t\tif err != nil {\n1391: \t\t\tcontinue\n1392: \t\t}\n1393: \n1394: \t\t// If this is a map, it is checking the entire map value for equality\n1395: \t\t// rather than the individual key. This means that the change is stored\n1396: \t\t// here even if our ignored key doesn't change. That is OK since it\n1397: \t\t// won't cause any changes in the transformation, but allows us to skip\n1398: \t\t// breaking up the maps and checking for key existence here too.\n1399: \t\tif !p.RawEquals(c) {\n1400: \t\t\t// there a change to ignore at this path, store the prior value\n1401: \t\t\tignoredValues = append(ignoredValues, ignoreChange{icPath, p, key})\n1402: \t\t}\n1403: \t}\n1404: \n1405: \tif len(ignoredValues) == 0 {\n1406: \t\treturn config, nil\n1407: \t}\n1408: \n1409: \tret, _ := cty.Transform(config, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1410: \t\t// Easy path for when we are only matching the entire value. The only\n1411: \t\t// values we break up for inspection are maps.\n1412: \t\tif !v.Type().IsMapType() {\n1413: \t\t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1414: \t\t\t\tif path.Equals(ignored.path) {\n1415: \t\t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1416: \t\t\t\t}\n1417: \t\t\t}\n1418: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1419: \t\t}\n1420: \t\t// We now know this must be a map, so we need to accumulate the values\n1421: \t\t// key-by-key.\n1422: \n1423: \t\tif !v.IsNull() && !v.IsKnown() {\n1424: \t\t\t// since v is not known, we cannot ignore individual keys\n1425: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1426: \t\t}\n1427: \n1428: \t\t// The map values will remain as cty values, so we only need to store\n1429: \t\t// the marks from the outer map itself\n1430: \t\tv, vMarks := v.Unmark()\n1431: \n1432: \t\t// The configMap is the current configuration value, which we will\n1433: \t\t// mutate based on the ignored paths and the prior map value.\n1434: \t\tvar configMap map[string]cty.Value\n1435: \t\tswitch {\n1436: \t\tcase v.IsNull() || v.LengthInt() == 0:\n1437: \t\t\tconfigMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1438: \t\tdefault:\n1439: \t\t\tconfigMap = v.AsValueMap()\n1440: \t\t}\n1441: \n1442: \t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1443: \t\t\tif !path.Equals(ignored.path) {\n1444: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1445: \t\t\t}\n1446: \n1447: \t\t\tif ignored.key.IsNull() {\n1448: \t\t\t\t// The map address is confirmed to match at this point,\n1449: \t\t\t\t// so if there is no key, we want the entire map and can\n1450: \t\t\t\t// stop accumulating values.\n1451: \t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1452: \t\t\t}\n1453: \t\t\t// Now we know we are ignoring a specific index of this map, so get\n1454: \t\t\t// the config map and modify, add, or remove the desired key.\n1455: \n1456: \t\t\t// We also need to create a prior map, so we can check for\n1457: \t\t\t// existence while getting the value, because Value.Index will\n1458: \t\t\t// return null for a key with a null value and for a non-existent\n1459: \t\t\t// key.\n1460: \t\t\tvar priorMap map[string]cty.Value\n1461: \n1462: \t\t\t// We need to drop the marks from the ignored map for handling. We\n1463: \t\t\t// don't need to store these, as we now know the ignored value is\n1464: \t\t\t// only within the map, not the map itself.\n1465: \t\t\tignoredVal, _ := ignored.value.Unmark()\n1466: \n1467: \t\t\tswitch {\n1468: \t\t\tcase ignored.value.IsNull() || ignoredVal.LengthInt() == 0:\n1469: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1470: \t\t\tdefault:\n1471: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = \t\t\t\t// this didn't exist in the old map value, so we're keeping the\n1480: \t\t\t\t// \"absence\" of the key by removing it from the config\n1481: \t\t\t\tdelete(configMap, key)\n1482: \t\t\tdefault:\n1483: \t\t\t\tconfigMap[key] = priorElem\n1484: \t\t\t}\n1485: \t\t}\n1486: \n1487: \t\tvar newVal cty.Value\n1488: \t\tswitch {\n1489: \t\tcase len(configMap) > 0:\n1490: \t\t\tnewVal = cty.MapVal(configMap)\n1491: \t\tcase v.IsNull():\n1492: \t\t\t// if the config value was null, and no values remain in the map,\n1493: \t\t\t// reset the value to null.\n1494: \t\t\tnewVal = v\n1495: \t\tdefault:\n1496: \t\t\tnewVal = cty.MapValEmpty(v.Type().ElementType())\n1497: \t\t}\n1498: \n1499: \t\tif len(vMarks) > 0 {\n1500: \t\t\tnewVal = newVal.WithMarks(vMarks)\n1501: \t\t}\n1502: \n1503: \t\treturn newVal, nil\n1504: \t})\n1505: \treturn ret, nil\n1506: }\n1507: \n1508: // readDataSource handles everything needed to call ReadDataSource on the provider.\n1509: // A previously evaluated configVal can be passed in, or a new one is generated\n1510: // from the resource configuration.\n1511: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) readDataSource(ctx EvalContext, is\n1677: // returned. It embeds NodeAbstractResource but additionally\\n30: // contains an instance key, used to identify one of potentially many\\n31: // instances that were created from a resource in configuration, e.g. using\\n32: // the \\\"count\\\" or \\\"for_each\\\" arguments.\\n33: type NodeAbstractResourceInstance struct {\\n34: \\tNodeAbstractResource\\n35: \\tAddr addrs.AbsResourceInstance\\n36: \\n37: \\t// These are set via the AttachState method.\\n38: \\tinstanceState *states.ResourceInstance\\n39: \\n40: \\tDependencies []addrs.ConfigResource\\n41: \\n42: \\tpreDestroyRefresh bool\\n43: \\n44: \\t// During import we may generate configuration for a resource, which needs\\n45: \\t// to be stored in the final change.\\n46: \\tgeneratedConfigHCL string\\n47: \\n48: \\t// override is set by the graph itself, just before this node executes.\\n49: \\toverride *configs.Override\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // NewNodeAbstractResourceInstance creates an abstract resource instance graph\\n53: // node for the given absolute resource instance address.\\n54: func NewNodeAbstractResourceInstance(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance) *NodeAbstractResourceInstance {\\n55: \\t// Due to the fact that we embed NodeAbstractResource, the given address\\n56: \\t// actually ends up split between the resource address in the embedded\\n57: \\t// object and the InstanceKey field in our own struct. This mark asymmetry is never stored in state, causing subsequent plan comparisons to detect differences in sensitivity metadata even when attribute values are identical. Additionally, the state file's `sensitive_attributes` records incomplete sensitivity information, omitting schema-defined sensitive paths entirely.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause spans a **sensitivity mark gap** across four interconnected mechanisms:\n\n1. **Provider responses lack all sensitivity information** — providers return unmarked values\n2. **Mark reconstruction omits schema-defined sensitive attributes** — only config-source marks are re-applied\n3. **State serialization captures incomplete marks** — `AttrSensitivePaths` only contains marks explicitly on the in-memory value\n4. **Plan comparison detects mark differences as attribute changes** — causes NoOp to become Update\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. Provider Response Flow (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:902-916)\n\nThe provider's `PlanResourceChange` is called with unmarked values and returns unmarked responses:\n\n```go\nresp = provider.PlanResourceChange(providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest{\n    TypeName:         n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n    Config:           unmarkedConfigVal,\n    PriorState:       unmarkedPriorVal,\n    ProposedNewState: proposedNewVal,\n    PriorPrivate:     priorPrivate,\n    ProviderMeta:     metaConfigVal,\n})\nplannedNewVal := resp.PlannedState  // <-- NO marks from provider\n```\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:902-916`\n**Line 916:** Provider response received without any sensitivity marks\n\n### 2. Configuration-Only Mark Reconstruction (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:868, 998-999)\n\nMarks from the **configuration** are extracted before provider call and re-applied afterward, but these represent only **variable-source sensitivity**, not schema-defined sensitivity:\n\n```go\n// Line 868: Extract config marks before sending to provider\nunmarkedConfigVal, unmarkedPaths := configValIgnored.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n// Lines 998-999: Re-apply config marks ONLY\nif len(unmarkedPaths) > 0 {\n    plannedNewVal = plannedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(unmarkedPaths)\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:868, 998-999`\n**Key Issue:** `unmarkedPaths` contains marks from sensitive variable references (e.g., `var.db_password` is marked sensitive), but NOT marks from provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations.\n\n### 3. State Serialization with Incomplete Marks (instance_object.go:94-136)\n\nWhen encoding the planned state object to state, marks are extracted from the value itself. Since schema marks were never applied to the value, they're not captured:\n\n```go\nfunc (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\n    // Line 98: Extract marks from the value\n    val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n    // Lines 128-136: Save only marks that were on the value\n    return &ResourceInstanceObjectSrc{\n        SchemaVersion:       schemaVersion,\n        AttrsJSON:           src,\n        AttrSensitivePaths:  pvm,  // <-- INCOMPLETE: missing schema-defined marks\n        Private:             o.Private,\n        Status:              o.Status,\n        Dependencies:        dependencies,\n        CreateBeforeDestroy: o.CreateBeforeDestroy,\n    }, nil\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `internal/states/instance_object.go:94-136`\n**Key Issue:** `pvm` only contains marks that were explicitly set on `o.Value`. Schema-defined sensitivity is never on the value, so it's not saved to state.\n\n### 4. State Decoding with Incomplete Marks (instance_object_src.go:77-103)\n\nWhen state is read back, only the incomplete marks from `AttrSensitivePaths` are re-applied:\n\n```go\nfunc (os *ResourceInstanceObjectSrc) Decode(ty cty.Type) (*ResourceInstanceObject, error) {\n    // Line 87: Unmarshal JSON\n    val, err = ctyjson.Unmarshal(os.AttrsJSON, ty)\n    // Lines 89-90: Apply ONLY stored marks (incomplete)\n    if os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n        val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)\n    }\n    if err != nil {\n        return nil, err\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `internal/states/instance_object_src.go:77-103**\n**Key Issue:** Decoded values lack schema-defined sensitivity marks because they were never stored in state.\n\n### 5. Phantom Update Detection (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208)\n\nThe plan compares marks from prior state against marks from planned value. When schema marks differ, a NoOp becomes an Update:\n\n```go\n// Line 1208: The phantom update mechanism\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208`\n**Explanation:**\n- `plannedNewVal` has marks from `unmarkedPaths` (config-source only, from line 999)\n- `priorPaths` has marks extracted from decoded state (also incomplete, from line 869)\n- If schema marks should apply to `plannedNewVal` but don't, or if they should apply to `priorPaths` but don't, comparison fails\n- Even though underlying values are identical, mark difference triggers Update action\n\n### 6. The Compensating Workaround (evaluate.go:714-723, 689-693)\n\n**Only** when reading from state for expression evaluation does Terraform compensate by re-applying schema marks:\n\n```go\n// Lines 714-723: Re-applying schema marks for expressions\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/evaluate.go:714-723`\n**Key Issue:** This happens ONLY during expression evaluation (`GetResource()`), not during plan construction or state serialization. This creates an asymmetry:\n- Values in state ≠ Values during expression evaluation (marks differ)\n- This workaround prevents expressions from seeing incomplete marks, but does nothing for plan comparison\n\n### 7. The underlying state file lacks this information entirely (internal/command/jsonstate/state.go:402-406 does the same workaround).\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Core Flow\n- **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`** — Plan construction, provider response handling, mark reconstruction\n- **`internal/states/instance_object.go`** — State encoding, mark extraction\n- **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`** — State decoding, mark application\n- **`internal/terraform/marks.go`** — Mark comparison logic (`marksEqual`, `filterMarks`)\n\n### Evaluation & Compensation\n- **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** — Expression evaluation context, schema mark re-application workaround\n- **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract.go`** — State reading for evaluation\n\n### JSON Output (Manifestation)\n- **`internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go`** — Plan JSON marshaling, redundant schema mark re-application\n- **`internal/command/jsonstate/state.go`** — State JSON marshaling, redundant schema mark re-application\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Provider Response** → Returns unmarked value (provider responsibility)\n\n2. **Configuration Mark Extraction** → Extracts marks from config: only variable-source marks captured\n   - Underlying values identical\n   - Marks differ (incomplete in state, complete in expression evaluator only)\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Root Fix Strategy:**\n\n1. **Preserve schema sensitivity in state** — When encoding to state, add schema-defined sensitive paths to `AttrSensitivePaths` before serialization\n   - These compensations exist because marks were incomplete; fixing source eliminates the need\n\n3. **Consistent mark handling in plan construction** — Ensure that `plannedNewVal` receives schema marks the same way prior values do\n   - Configuration-Only Mark Reconstruction (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:868, 998-999)\n\nMarks from the **configuration** are extracted before provider call and re-applied afterward, but these represent only **variable-source sensitivity**, not schema-defined sensitivity:\n\n```go\n// Line 868: Extract config marks before sending to provider\nunmarkedConfigVal, unmarkedPaths := configValIgnored.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n// Lines 998-999: Re-apply config marks ONLY\nif len(unmarkedPaths) > 0 {\n    plannedNewVal = plannedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(unmarkedPaths)\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:868, 998-999`\n**Key Issue:** `unmarkedPaths` contains marks from sensitive variable references (e.g., `var.db_password` is marked sensitive), but NOT marks from provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations.\n\n### 3. State Serialization with Incomplete Marks (instance_object.go:94-136)\n\nWhen encoding the planned state object to state, marks are extracted from the value itself. Since schema marks were never applied to the value, they're not captured:\n\n```go\nfunc (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\n    // Line 98: Extract marks from the value\n    val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n    // Lines 128-136: Save only marks that were on the value\n    return &ResourceInstanceObjectSrc{\n        SchemaVersion:       schemaVersion,\n        AttrsJSON:           src,\n        AttrSensitivePaths:  pvm,  // <-- INCOMPLETE: missing schema-defined marks\n        Private:             o.Private,\n        Status:              o.Status,\n        Dependencies:        dependencies,\n        CreateBeforeDestroy: o.CreateBeforeDestroy,\n    }, nil\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `internal/states/instance_object.go:94-136`\n**Key Issue:** `pvm` only contains marks that were explicitly set on `o.Value`. Schema-defined sensitivity is never on the value, so it's not saved to state.\n\n### 4. State Decoding with Incomplete Marks (instance_object_src.go:77-103)\n\nWhen state is read back, only the incomplete marks from `AttrSensitivePaths` are re-applied:\n\n```go\nfunc (os *ResourceInstanceObjectSrc) Decode(ty cty.Type) (*ResourceInstanceObject, error) {\n    // Line 87: Unmarshal JSON\n    val, err = ctyjson.Unmarshal(os.AttrsJSON, ty)\n    // Lines 89-90: Apply ONLY stored marks (incomplete)\n    if os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n        val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)\n    }\n    if err != nil {\n        return nil, err\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `internal/states/instance_object_src.go:77-103**\n**Key Issue:** Decoded values lack schema-defined sensitivity marks because they were never stored in state.\n\n### 5. Phantom Update Detection (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208)\n\nThe plan compares marks from prior state against marks from planned value. When schema marks differ, a NoOp becomes an Update:\n\n```go\n// Line 1208: The phantom update mechanism\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208`\n**Explanation:**\n- `plannedNewVal` has marks from `unmarkedPaths` (config-source only, from line 999)\n- `priorPaths` has marks extracted from decoded state (also incomplete, from line 869)\n- If schema marks should apply to `plannedNewVal` but don't, or if they should apply to `priorPaths` but don't, comparison fails\n- Even though underlying values are identical, mark difference triggers Update action\n\n### 6. The Compensating Workaround (evaluate.go:714-723, 689-693)\n\n**Only** when reading from state for expression evaluation does Terraform compensate by re-applying schema marks:\n\n```go\n// Lines 714-723: Re-applying schema marks for expressions\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/evaluate.go:714-723`\n**Key Issue:** This happens ONLY during expression evaluation (`GetResource()`), not during plan construction or state serialization. This creates an asymmetry:\n- Values in state ≠ Values during expression evaluation (marks differ)\n- This workaround prevents expressions from seeing incomplete marks, but does nothing for plan comparison\n\n### 7. JSON Output Manifestation (jsonplan/plan.go:417-419, 446-448)\n\nJSON plan and state output attempt to apply schema marks, but the underlying state is incomplete:\n\n```go\n// Lines 417-419: BeforeSensitive in JSON output\nmarks := rc.BeforeValMarks\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(changeV.Before, nil)...)\n}\n\n// Lines 446-448: AfterSensitive in JSON output\nmarks := rc.AfterValMarks\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(changeV.After, nil)...)\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go:417-419, 446-448`\n**Key Issue:** JSON output produces correct sensitivity maps by re-applying schema marks, but this is redundant work and indicates marks were never preserved. The underlying state file lacks this information entirely (internal/command/jsonstate/state.go:402-406 does the same workaround).\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Core Flow\n- **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`** — Plan construction, provider response handling, mark reconstruction\n- **`internal/states/instance_object.go`** — State encoding, mark extraction\n- **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`** — State decoding, mark application\n- **`internal/terraform/marks.go`** — Mark comparison logic (`marksEqual`, `filterMarks`)\n\n### Evaluation & Compensation\n- **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** — Expression evaluation context, schema mark re-application workaround\n- **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract.go`** — State reading for evaluation\n\n### JSON Output (Manifestation)\n- **`internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go`** — Plan JSON marshaling, redundant schema mark re-application\n- **`internal/command/jsonstate/state.go`** — State JSON marshaling, redundant schema mark re-application\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Provider Response** → Returns unmarked value (provider responsibility)\n\n2. **Configuration Mark Extraction** → Extracts marks from config: only variable-source marks captured\n   - File: `node_resource_abstract_instance.go:868` (`unmarkedPaths`)\n\n3. **Config Mark Re-application** → Re-applies only config marks to planned value\n   - File: `node_resource_abstract_instance.go:998-999`\n   - Missing: Schema marks never re-applied\n\n4. **Change Construction** → Planned value stored in change with incomplete marks\n   - File: `node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1236-1247`\n\n5. **State Encoding** → Marks extracted from planned value, only config marks saved\n   - File: `instance_object.go:98-131`\n   - State file contains `AttrSensitivePaths` with only config-source marks\n\n6. **State Decoding** → Marks restored from state (incomplete)\n   - File: `instance_object_src.go:87-90`\n   - Schema marks missing from decoded value\n\n7. **Plan Comparison** → Detects mark difference between planned and prior\n   - File: `node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208`\n   - NoOp → Update due to missing schema marks\n\n8. **Symptom Manifest** → Plan shows phantom update\n   - Underlying values identical\n   - Marks differ (incomplete in state, complete in expression evaluator only)\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Root Fix Strategy:**\n\n1. **Preserve schema sensitivity in state** — When encoding to state, add schema-defined sensitive paths to `AttrSensitivePaths` before serialization\n   - Modify: `instance_object.go:Encode()` to apply schema marks before `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`\n   - Alternative: Store schema sensitivity separately in state file format\n\n2. **Eliminate redundant mark compensation** — Once schema marks are stored, remove the workaround logic from `evaluate.go`, `jsonplan/plan.go`, and `jsonstate/state.go`\n   - These compensations exist because marks were incomplete; fixing source eliminates the need\n\n3. **Consistent mark handling in plan construction** — Ensure that `plannedNewVal` receives schema marks the same way prior values do\n   - Both prior and planned should apply schema marks at the same point in the flow\n\n**Diagnostic Steps:**\n\n1. Add logging to `instance_object.go:Encode()` to show which marks are captured vs. missing\n2. Add logging to `node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208` to show why `marksEqual()` fails\n3.
